          --monorail-metadata-toggled-bg: var(--monorail-metadata-closed-bg);
        }
        mr-issue-page[codeFont] {
          --mr-toggled-font-family: Monospace;
        }
        .container-issue {
          width: 100%;
          flex-direction: column;
          align-items: stretch;
          justify-content: flex-start;
          z-index: 200;
        }
        .container-issue-content {
          padding: 0;
          flex-grow: 1;

        }
        .container-outside {
          box-sizing: border-box;
          width: 100%;
          max-width: 100%;
          margin: auto;
          padding: 0;
          display: flex;
          align-items: stretch;
          justify-content: space-between;
          flex-direction: row;
          flex-wrap: no-wrap;
        }
        .container-no-issue {
          padding: 0.5em 16px;
          font-size: var(--chops-large-font-size);
        }
        .metadata-container {
          font-size: var(--chops-main-font-size);

          border-right: var(--chops-normal-border);

          width: 24em;
          min-width: 256px;
          flex-grow: 0;
          flex-shrink: 0;
          box-sizing: border-box;
          z-index: 100;
        }
        .issue-header-container {

          top: var(--monorail-header-height);
          margin-bottom: 0.25em;
          width: 100%;
        }

          min-width: 50%;
          max-width: 1000px;
          flex-grow: 1;

          min-height: 100%;

          padding-right: var(--mr-issue-page-horizontal-padding);
        }
        mr-issue-metadata {
          position: sticky;
          overflow-y: auto;
          top: var(--monorail-header-height);
          height: calc(100vh - var(--monorail-header-height));
        }
        mr-launch-overview {
          border-left: var(--chops-normal-border);

          }
          mr-issue-details, mr-launch-overview {
            width: 100%;

        @media (max-width: 840px) {

          }
        }

Email display settings

<h2>Email display settings</h2>



        

There is a 

setting

<a href="/hosting/settings">setting</a>

 to control how
        your email address appears on comments and issues that you post.

<p>There is a <a href="/hosting/settings">setting</a> to control how
        your email address appears on comments and issues that you post.</p>



        

Project members will always see your full email address.  By
        default, other users who visit the site will see an
        abbreviated version of your email address.

<p>Project members will always see your full email address.  By
        default, other users who visit the site will see an
        abbreviated version of your email address.</p>



        

If you do not wish your email address to be shared, there
        are other ways to 

get
        involved

<a href="http://www.chromium.org/getting-involved">get
        involved</a>

 in the community.  To report a problem when using
        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item
        on the "Help" menu.

<p>If you do not wish your email address to be shared, there
        are other ways to <a href="http://www.chromium.org/getting-involved">get
        involved</a> in the community.  To report a problem when using
        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item
        on the "Help" menu.</p>

        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item
        on the "Help" menu.</p>

This site hosts public issues in public projects

<h2>This site hosts public issues in public projects</h2>



        

Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.

<p>Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.</p>



        

Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.

<p>Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.</p>

        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.</p>

        <p>Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.</p>

VULNERABILITY DETAILS



<b class="line"><!---->VULNERABILITY DETAILS<!----></b>



<br>





A page can use a carefully-sized popup combined with a pointer lock to force the user to select an autofill item with three consecutive clicks, without moving their mouse or pressing keyboard keys.



<span class="line"><!---->A page can use a carefully-sized popup combined with a pointer lock to force the user to select an autofill item with three consecutive clicks, without moving their mouse or pressing keyboard keys.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Normally Chrome requires an intentional selection by the user, either by moving the mouse over an autofill item or using the keyboard to select an autofill item.



<span class="line"><!---->Normally Chrome requires an intentional selection by the user, either by moving the mouse over an autofill item or using the keyboard to select an autofill item.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





The PoC works because requesting pointer lock in a small window will set the cursor to approximately the center of the content area while pointer lock is enabled. If the cursor location coincides with an autofill prompt item, the item will be highlighted, therefore an attacker can arrange the page so the autofill prompt is shown where the cursor is expected. The autofill prompt also accept clicks while pointer lock is enabled, so the user is able to click on the forced selection. With this last click, the browser provides the autofill data to the page.



<span class="line"><!---->The PoC works because requesting pointer lock in a small window will set the cursor to approximately the center of the content area while pointer lock is enabled. If the cursor location coincides with an autofill prompt item, the item will be highlighted, therefore an attacker can arrange the page so the autofill prompt is shown where the cursor is expected. The autofill prompt also accept clicks while pointer lock is enabled, so the user is able to click on the forced selection. With this last click, the browser provides the autofill data to the page.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





A user who clicks more slowly or is more observant may stop prior to the last click. However, because of the pointer lock it may be initially confusing on how to escape, and they may accidentally select the item. If a user tried to move their mouse and click repeatedly to find their cursor (which may occur instinctively despite browser providing escape instructions moments before), they're very likely to accidentally select an autofill item since the prompt covers most of the window and mouse movements are bounded to the window. 



<span class="line"><!---->A user who clicks more slowly or is more observant may stop prior to the last click. However, because of the pointer lock it may be initially confusing on how to escape, and they may accidentally select the item. If a user tried to move their mouse and click repeatedly to find their cursor (which may occur instinctively despite browser providing escape instructions moments before), they're very likely to accidentally select an autofill item since the prompt covers most of the window and mouse movements are bounded to the window. <!----></span>



<br>



<br>





I've tested this with addresses (which includes name + email) and credit cards. For sample input, see the video recording.



<span class="line"><!---->I've tested this with addresses (which includes name + email) and credit cards. For sample input, see the video recording.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





VERSION



<b class="line"><!---->VERSION<!----></b>



<br>





Chrome Version: 92.0.4515.131 (Official Build) (64-bit) (cohort: Stable), 94.0.4605.0 Canary



<span class="line"><!---->Chrome Version: 92.0.4515.131 (Official Build) (64-bit) (cohort: Stable), 94.0.4605.0 Canary<!----></span>



<br>





Operating System: Windows 10 OS Version 2009 (Build 19042.1110)



<span class="line"><!---->Operating System: Windows 10 OS Version 2009 (Build 19042.1110)<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





REPRODUCTION CASE



<b class="line"><!---->REPRODUCTION CASE<!----></b>



<br>





PoC for address:



<span class="line"><!---->PoC for address:<!----></span>



<br>





Prerequisite: Have at least one address with email address in chrome://settings/addresses



<span class="line"><!---->Prerequisite: Have at least one address with email address in chrome://settings/addresses<!----></span>



<br>





1. Navigate to 



<span class="line"><!---->1. Navigate to <!----></span>





https://alesandroortiz.com/security/chromium/autofill-pointer-lock.html



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://alesandroortiz.com/security/chromium/autofill-pointer-lock.html"><!---->https://alesandroortiz.com/security/chromium/autofill-pointer-lock.html<!----></a>



<br>





2. Click the same place three times in a row, anywhere in the page.



<span class="line"><!---->2. Click the same place three times in a row, anywhere in the page.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





PoC for credit card:



<span class="line"><!---->PoC for credit card:<!----></span>



<br>





Prerequisite: Have at least one credit card in chrome://settings/payments



<span class="line"><!---->Prerequisite: Have at least one credit card in chrome://settings/payments<!----></span>



<br>





1. Navigate to 



<span class="line"><!---->1. Navigate to <!----></span>





https://alesandroortiz.com/security/chromium/autofill-pointer-lock.html?creditcard



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://alesandroortiz.com/security/chromium/autofill-pointer-lock.html?creditcard"><!---->https://alesandroortiz.com/security/chromium/autofill-pointer-lock.html?creditcard<!----></a>



<br>





2. (Same as prior PoC, click three times in a row)



<span class="line"><!---->2. (Same as prior PoC, click three times in a row)<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





For all PoCs:



<span class="line"><!---->For all PoCs:<!----></span>



<br>





Observed: Autofilled data is provided to page, because pointer lock allows page to select an autofill item by moving the cursor over the autofill prompt, without any mouse movement or keyboard input.



<span class="line"><!---->Observed: Autofilled data is provided to page, because pointer lock allows page to select an autofill item by moving the cursor over the autofill prompt, without any mouse movement or keyboard input.<!----></span>



<br>





Expected: Autofilled data is *not* provided to page, because page cannot select an autofill item without user intentionally moving mouse or using keyboard to select item.



<span class="line"><!---->Expected: Autofilled data is *not* provided to page, because page cannot select an autofill item without user intentionally moving mouse or using keyboard to select item.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>

Thanks for your report, I'm not sure if this is an issue with pointerlock or one with autofill :) It seems perhaps the autofill UI shouldn't accept clicks if pointerlock is enabled but I wouldn't know what kind of use-cases that change would break.



<span class="line"><!---->Thanks for your report, I'm not sure if this is an issue with pointerlock or one with autofill :) It seems perhaps the autofill UI shouldn't accept clicks if pointerlock is enabled but I wouldn't know what kind of use-cases that change would break.<!----></span>

I'm adding some folks from the teams to take a look.

I have looked into this bug.



<span class="line"><!---->I have looked into this bug.<!----></span>



<br>





The bug doesn't repro on Mac or Linux.



<span class="line"><!---->The bug doesn't repro on Mac or Linux.<!----></span>



<br>





It repros only on Windows.



<span class="line"><!---->It repros only on Windows.<!----></span>



<br>





On Mac and Linux, PointerLock does lock the pointer, and the user cannot move it to select an item,



<span class="line"><!---->On Mac and Linux, PointerLock does lock the pointer, and the user cannot move it to select an item,<!----></span>



<br>





However on Windows, the user is able to move the pointer!



<span class="line"><!---->However on Windows, the user is able to move the pointer!<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





This looks like a PointerLock issue to me.



<span class="line"><!---->This looks like a PointerLock issue to me.<!----></span>

#c5



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="#c5"><!---->#c5<!----></a>

On Windows when the pointer is locked we basically hide the cursor, then constantly reset the pointer location to the center of the page. The key here is that all pointer events(including click) should be routed to the element that holds the lock so you should not be able to click on anything. 



<span class="line"><!---->On Windows when the pointer is locked we basically hide the cursor, then constantly reset the pointer location to the center of the page. The key here is that all pointer events(including click) should be routed to the element that holds the lock so you should not be able to click on anything. <!----></span>



<br>



<br>





I only worked on Pointer Lock to add the unadjusted movement capability.  Mustaq and his team own this API.



<span class="line"><!---->I only worked on Pointer Lock to add the unadjusted movement capability.  Mustaq and his team own this API.<!----></span>

<br>


    


        


      


        









The root cause here is that the auto-fill dialog is not aware of an active pointer-lock, and a click through a hidden+locked mouse cursor is treated as a click on the auto-fill dialog if the coordinates are correct.



<span class="line"><!---->The root cause here is that the auto-fill dialog is not aware of an active pointer-lock, and a click through a hidden+locked mouse cursor is treated as a click on the auto-fill dialog if the coordinates are correct.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





The repro works as follows:



<span class="line"><!---->The repro works as follows:<!----></span>



<br>





A. First click open a small window around the click position so that subsequent clicks to the opened window.  The window size is made small enough so that the same click position falls within the auto-fill dialog for that small window.



<span class="line"><!---->A. First click open a small window around the click position so that subsequent clicks to the opened window.  The window size is made small enough so that the same click position falls within the auto-fill dialog for that small window.<!----></span>



<br>





B. The second click goes to the small window and locks the mouse pointer there.



<span class="line"><!---->B. The second click goes to the small window and locks the mouse pointer there.<!----></span>



<br>





C. The third click selects an auto-fill option.



<span class="line"><!---->C. The third click selects an auto-fill option.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





This didn't repro for me on Linux or CrOS, and 



<span class="line"><!---->This didn't repro for me on Linux or CrOS, and <!----></span>





#c8



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="#c8"><!---->#c8<!----></a>





 mentioned the same about Mac.



<span class="line"><!----> mentioned the same about Mac.<!----></span>

I reached the same conclusion as wfh@ above: making auto-fill dialog not responding to locked mouse seems like a logical fix here.  But I find the repro not very easily reproducible without the user's notice, so I think P2 is the right priority here.



<span class="line"><!---->I reached the same conclusion as wfh@ above: making auto-fill dialog not responding to locked mouse seems like a logical fix here.  But I find the repro not very easily reproducible without the user's notice, so I think P2 is the right priority here.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Assigning the bug back to mamir@ because I don't know much about autofill UI.  I will be happy to help with pointer-lock state related question.



<span class="line"><!---->Assigning the bug back to mamir@ because I don't know much about autofill UI.  I will be happy to help with pointer-lock state related question.<!----></span>

[Autofill] Hide Autofill popup if the mouse pointer is locked.



<span class="line"><!---->[Autofill] Hide Autofill popup if the mouse pointer is locked.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





This CL hides the Autofill popup when the underlying frame holds a



<span class="line"><!---->This CL hides the Autofill popup when the underlying frame holds a<!----></span>



<br>





pointer lock.



<span class="line"><!---->pointer lock.<!----></span>



<br>

schwering@: Thanks for landing the fix. While trying to verify on ASan (too impatient to wait for tomorrow's Canary), I encountered a couple of potentially new stability issues. These *might* be pre-existing issues that could already be triggered in other ways, but the fix made it possible to trigger them with the PoCs below.

<span class="line"><!---->Can you reproduce the issues with an earlier ASan build that does not contain the patch from <!----></span>





#c20



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="#c20"><!---->#c20<!----></a>





 if, right after the Autofill popup occurs, you press Escape? The reason I'm asking: Escape hides the Autofill popup, and the patch does pretty much the same as pressing Escape: it hides the popup if the frame holds a pointer lock and either (a) the popup is about to be shown or (b) a suggestion is selected (= mouse moves over a row) or (c) a suggestion is accepted (= mouse clicks on a row) or (d) a suggestion is removed (= DEL is pressed while a row is selected). Conditions (b)–(d) can be exactly replicated with Escape. Only Condition (a) is not reproducible with Escape because the popup is not even shown.



<span class="line"><!----> if, right after the Autofill popup occurs, you press Escape? The reason I'm asking: Escape hides the Autofill popup, and the patch does pretty much the same as pressing Escape: it hides the popup if the frame holds a pointer lock and either (a) the popup is about to be shown or (b) a suggestion is selected (= mouse moves over a row) or (c) a suggestion is accepted (= mouse clicks on a row) or (d) a suggestion is removed (= DEL is pressed while a row is selected). Conditions (b)–(d) can be exactly replicated with Escape. Only Condition (a) is not reproducible with Escape because the popup is not even shown.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





It looks to me like the issues are surfaced by

[Autofill] Check for self-destruction after selecting a suggestions.

<br>





This UAF was introduced in



<span class="line"><!---->This UAF was introduced in<!----></span>





 



<span class="line"><!----> <!----></span>





crrev.com/c/3297919



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://crrev.com/c/3297919"><!---->crrev.com/c/3297919<!----></a>





 by hiding the popup



<span class="line"><!----> by hiding the popup<!----></span>



<br>





in SetSelectedLine() if the window holds a pointer lock. Since hiding



<span class="line"><!---->in SetSelectedLine() if the window holds a pointer lock. Since hiding<!----></span>



<br>





the popup deletes the popup, |this| must not be accessed afterwards.



<span class="line"><!---->the popup deletes the popup, |this| must not be accessed afterwards.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





This CL is a quick fix that adds checks after calling SetSelectedLine().



<span class="line"><!---->This CL is a quick fix that adds checks after calling SetSelectedLine().<!----></span>



<br>





The followup CLs will make this and other checks for weak_this



<span class="line"><!---->The followup CLs will make this and other checks for weak_this<!----></span>

<span class="line"><!---->redundant:<!----></span>

*** Boilerplate reminders! ***



<span class="line"><!---->*** Boilerplate reminders! ***<!----></span>



<br>





Please do NOT publicly disclose details until a fix has been released to all our users. Early public disclosure may cancel the provisional reward. Also, please be considerate about disclosure when the bug affects a core library that may be used by other products. Please do NOT share this information with third parties who are not directly involved in fixing the bug. Doing so may cancel the provisional reward. Please be honest if you have already disclosed anything publicly or to third parties. Lastly, we understand that some of you are not interested in money. We offer the option to donate your reward to an eligible charity. If you prefer this option, let us know and we will also match your donation - subject to our discretion. Any rewards that are unclaimed after 12 months will be donated to a charity of our choosing.

        /*
         * Really specific class names are necessary because ShadowDOM
         * is disabled for this component.
         */
        .chops-autocomplete-container {
          position: relative;
        }
        .chops-autocomplete-container table {
          padding: 0;
          font-size: var(--chops-main-font-size);
          color: var(--chops-link-color);
          position: absolute;
          background: var(--chops-white);
          border: var(--chops-accessible-border);
          z-index: 999;
          box-shadow: 2px 3px 8px 0px hsla(0, 0%, 0%, 0.3);
          border-spacing: 0;
          border-collapse: collapse;
          /* In the case when the autocomplete extends the
           * height of the viewport, we want to make sure
           * there's spacing. */
          margin-bottom: 1em;
        }
        .chops-autocomplete-container tbody {
          display: block;
          min-width: 100px;
          max-height: 500px;
          overflow: auto;
        }
        .chops-autocomplete-container tr {
          cursor: pointer;
          transition: background 0.2s ease-in-out;
        }
        .chops-autocomplete-container tr[data-selected] {
          background: var(--chops-active-choice-bg);
          text-decoration: underline;
        }
        .chops-autocomplete-container td {
          padding: 0.25em 8px;
          white-space: nowrap;
        }
        .screenreader-hidden {
          clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);
          height: 1px;
          overflow: hidden;
          position: absolute;
          white-space: nowrap;
          width: 1px;
        }

          box-shadow: 2px 3px 8px 0px hsla(0, 0%, 0%, 0.3);
          border-spacing: 0;
          border-collapse: collapse;
          /* In the case when the autocomplete extends the
           * height of the viewport, we want to make sure
           * there's spacing. */
          margin-bottom: 1em;
        }
        .chops-autocomplete-container tbody {
          display: block;
          min-width: 100px;
          max-height: 500px;
          overflow: auto;
        }
        .chops-autocomplete-container tr {
          cursor: pointer;
          transition: background 0.2s ease-in-out;
        }
        .chops-autocomplete-container tr[data-selected] {
          background: var(--chops-active-choice-bg);
          text-decoration: underline;
        }
        .chops-autocomplete-container td {
          padding: 0.25em 8px;
          white-space: nowrap;
        }
        .screenreader-hidden {
          clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);
          height: 1px;
          overflow: hidden;
          position: absolute;
          white-space: nowrap;
          width: 1px;
        }
      </style>
      <div class="chops-autocomplete-container">
        <span class="screenreader-hidden" aria-live="polite">
          
        </span>
        <table hidden="">
          <tbody>
            
          </tbody>
        </table>
      </div>
    <!----></mr-autocomplete>
            </div>
          </div>

 }
 }
 });
